Free Talk

On Criticism

— Lin Huiyin

Mr. Du Heng recently saw a literary cartoon: it depicted a child tearing a book, and the caption was: "He will become a critic." He was moved by this and wrote an article about criticism. However, the cartoonist's opinion is debatable because the child tearing the book doesn't necessarily mean that he is tearing it because the content is bad, just as he might drop a bowl because he finds it adorable, and the sound of it breaking is pleasant. Therefore, tearing a book is not necessarily a sign that the child will become a critic.

Although, I would also like to say something about criticism.

Criticism is now generally regarded as a tool for revenge. Often, when people see criticism of their work, the first thing they notice is not the criticism itself, but the critic. If the critic is someone they know, they will reflect on whether they have offended them in any way. If they cannot think of any offense they have committed, they will not understand why the critic is criticizing their work. However, in the end, they are usually able to find a reason, such as a rejected submission or a denied loan. They will then state the reason to prove that the criticism is only meant to settle a private score, as if to say that it does not harm their work.

If the author does not know the critic but only knows about them, they will quickly look to see if the critic has a group behind them, or to see what the real intention of the criticism is. Once they believe they have seen things clearly, they can then point out to the readers that they should not be fooled by the critic, that the critic has a group behind them, or that the criticism has some other purpose. If the critic's signature is unfamiliar, the author will either assume that it is someone's pseudonym and launch a counterattack against the person hidden behind the pseudonym, or they will simply ignore it, implying that the criticism is without merit.

Because criticism is only seen as a way to settle private scores, responses to criticism easily degenerate into personal attacks. The person being criticized does not address the criticism itself, but only the critic's personal characteristics. If they know that the critic has a gray hair, or has lost sleep once, or even that their father was an opium smoker, they will attack that point, in order to prove that the critic is not qualified to criticize their work.

In fact, criticism is just criticism. Why not seek truth and falsehood in the criticism itself? Is criticism really only a tool for revenge? And even if there was indeed some private feud between the critic and the person being criticized, and the critic's motive for the criticism was indeed revenge, if the criticism is accurate, can the person being criticized dismiss the criticism by saying what the critic's motive is? Does ignoring the criticism conceal the errors that have been pointed out in their work? If the criticism is incorrect, they can simply state why it is incorrect, and where it is incorrect, without having to pay attention to whether the other party has gray hair or has had a submission rejected.

Criticism is just criticism; there is no need to involve anything else.

My Melancholy

— Jin Yi

Leaning alone in the train car, I am aimlessly carried by the train to any place, but my heart will not settle. Like a shadow, it follows me: my melancholy.

But I do not complain, because it is so faithful.

The sound of the wheels grinding against the rails seems to be disrupting my nerves, so I lower the window; but there is still that sound, faint as it is, it weighs heavily on my heart. I continue to read a novel translated by a friend that I have already read more than half of, a story about two lost children meeting. After finishing the book, my eyes are wet, and I want to have the chance to cry my heart out, but I can't do that, because I know the person sitting across from me is watching my eyes.

"Where is the place I am going to?"

I ask myself this question. I can only lower my head and wait for the train to enter the station. Among a crowd of people, I walk aimlessly. I arrive at my home, and my home becomes so desolate.

Although it is already dark, I still go out. I pull up the collar of my coat, braving the chill of late autumn, walking slowly and alone.

By the time I return to my home, it is two o'clock after midnight.

That evening, an old acquaintance, whom I met by chance at a friend's house, told me so many things. Her body was trembling as she spoke of many regrets and hopes. Such a stubborn woman had become so weak.

I, who have seen the world as so trivial, am told that I am getting old and useless; but when I walk back, I feel sympathy for her pitiable appearance. My melancholy becomes even more profound. I know that there is one more person in this world enduring suffering. I even hate myself. For humanitarian reasons, I should not have responded to her narrative with a cold smile. She scolded me, and thinking about it, it was not an overreaction; because I was so wooden, like withered and broken grass.

Now I have to laugh, but sometimes my laughter makes people so unhappy. This time she also said: "Can't you stop for a moment? You know I'm so nervous." I saw her body tremble, tremble so terribly, although I knew that perhaps some kind of change had taken place in her heart, but I deliberately talked about the weather. "Do you feel cold?"

"Yes, an unbearable cold."

"Me too," I smiled, "otherwise I would take off my coat and give it to you."

"You are cold!"

She said the word "cold" so heavily, I knew her intention, but at most I could only shake hands with her like a friend.

If there is a desire to save people, I myself should be the first to be saved!

Then she said sadly:

"Remember me a little, as a friend, I know you are a good man, I want you to always be a good man!"

She turned around and walked away, and in the darkness, her dark figure quickly disappeared.

I returned to my home, regretting that I had seen her or had not been able to do what she wanted.

I know I am old, but my melancholy is so young, so strong, pressing on my heart.

In the Teahouse

— Peng Chenghui

It was June, and the sun was burning on the ground like fire.

There was not a breath of fresh air, even though we were in these lush mountains. The tall pine trees and short bushes were quietly gasping for breath under the fierce sunlight. The surroundings were very silent, with only the raucous calls of partridges echoing in the valleys and the clear, babbling sound of a spring flowing beneath the rocky cliffs. Because the weather was too hot, there were very few passersby. Even the men carrying salted fish, bolts of cloth, and ramie were rarely seen, although this path was the only mountain trail from Fengshuzhai to Hetianxu.

There was a teahouse located along this secluded mountain path. The teahouse was very small, with only a main hall, no rooms, and no doors. Inside, apart from a few stone benches, there were only a few cow dung pellets and dry firewood ash as decorations. On the center wall were the three large characters "An Lv Ting" [Peaceful Journey Pavilion]. On either side was a couplet made of bricks: the right side read, "Busy for fame, busy for profit, steal a moment from the busy to have a cup of tea." The left side read, "Suffering for clothes, suffering for food, find joy in suffering, grab a pot of wine." It seemed that the teahouse had a long history and had weathered many years of wind and rain and the erosion of frost and snow, so it already appeared ancient and dilapidated.

Grandmother was very old. Her skin was wrinkled like citrus peel, her body bent like a bow. Hunched over, she would always sit in this teahouse, dozing off all day long. In front of her was a table made of wooden planks, on which were arranged ten or so packets of Yunpian cakes, three or four tubes of small biscuits, several bowls of clear tea, and a dozen or so pears. These foods awaiting the patronage of passersby were her purpose for staying here every day, rain or shine.

Our home was a few mud houses built on the mountainside in front. There, sparsely scattered, were only ten or so households. At the moment, it seemed that no one was cooking, and there was no smoke rising from the rooftops. I and Xiaoqiu had just returned from grazing the cows on the mountain, and our stomachs were growling fiercely. Seeing the things in front of Grandmother, I felt saliva welling up in my mouth like a spring. The snow-white Yunpian cakes, the round biscuits, and the yellow pears seemed to have an immense attraction, and my eyes kept darting around them, almost to the point of calculating the exact number of each.

"Grandma! Just let me eat one!" I finally couldn't help but speak.

"Eat what?" She seemed a little deaf and widened her old eyes.

"A pear!"

"No! These were bought with money."

"What does it matter if I eat just one!"

"One costs seven or eight copper coins."

"I'm starving to death!"

"They're cooking at home, go home to eat!"

"They haven't started cooking at home yet! Look, there's no smoke rising from the roof."

Although Grandmother was very determined not to let me eat, I always refused to listen and kept pestering her, as if she were old and easily bullied. It seemed she would always agree to my requests, even if she scolded me a few times; I wouldn't take it to heart. She stood up and rearranged the things that made me salivate, as if she was wary of me reaching out to grab them automatically. Hearing me say that there was no smoke rising from the roof at home, she actually raised her head and looked ahead into the distance with her dim eyes.

"They should be cooking soon," she explained slowly.

"No, I want to eat one! I want to eat one, I'm starving to death!" I clamored, as if I had to achieve my goal.

"You're really naughty! I told you not to eat, but you insist on eating. In that case, pick a small one, one with worms!" She seemed to be overwhelmed and finally agreed.

I immediately smiled and reached out to take one. It was not the smallest or worm-eaten one, but the biggest, roundest, and yellowest one. The fragrance immediately wafted into my nostrils.

"Xiaoqiu, let's go to the mountain ravine behind to rub river snails, and come back to eat lunch," I said to Xiaoqiu after taking a bite of the pear.

"Okay, let's go!" Xiaoqiu saw that I had a pear to eat and was beaming as if he would get a share. He jumped down from the stone slab happily.

"Naughty brat! You have to eat such a big one when you eat it yourself!..." I heard Grandmother complaining, but I ignored her and jumped away with Xiaoqiu into the mountains behind the teahouse without turning my head.

Literary Miscellany

— Meng Yuan

(Two)

Mr. Sun Fuxi, who travels frequently between Shanghai and Hangzhou, recently went to Suzhou again to give a lecture on "The Joys of Life." His lecture is published in the fifth issue of the second volume of "Literary Tea Talks." After Mr. Sun spoke about the joys of life, the first being mutual assistance and the second being universal love, he used current events to prove his point:

"Now, the loss of the four northeastern provinces is a great shame for China, and we must do our best to win them back. However (the article suddenly shifts here! Meng's note), this cannot be achieved by weeping and wailing all day long. We should happily increase our knowledge and skills to compete with our enemies (this is what is called saving the country by focusing on our own work! Meng's note). It is like if a classmate insults me, I do not have to insult him back in the same way. Besides reasoning with him (this reasoning is not about eating tea! Meng's third note), I must work even harder myself (for example, Mr. Sun does not listen to cannons, but writes exclusively about chrysanthemums! Meng's fourth note). This is also a method of revenge, and it contains a great joy in life (which can also be said to have political implications! Meng's fifth note)."

Mr. Sun's philosophy of saving the country can be seen here. It is a pity that this philosophy does not have a general name, which is a bit of a flaw. I would very much like to give it the name "Tea Talk Salvation Theory." People who support this view would be called "Tea Talk Salvationists." I wonder if that is appropriate? Since ancient times, although "pure talk" has repeatedly misled the country, this "tea talk" is fundamentally different from "pure talk," and I think it will definitely not cause misunderstandings in various circles.

The Two Brothers (60)

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

They now stood upright in the brackish puddle, the water up to their thighs, their hands dripping on the shrimp nets, their eyes locked on each other.

She said in a joking, argumentative tone:

"You really picked a great time to talk to me about this! Couldn't you have waited until some other time to say it, so as not to interfere with my shrimping?"

He murmured:

"I'm sorry, but I couldn't bear to keep it to myself any longer. I've loved you for a long time. Today, you've intoxicated me even more, and I've lost my reason."

Then, suddenly, she seemed to accept her fate, abandoned the pleasure of shrimping, and reluctantly started to talk about serious matters.

"Let's sit on that reef," she said. "We can talk in peace."

They climbed up the slightly higher rock, and as they sat side by side on it, bathed in the sun, their legs dangling, she spoke again:

"Dear friend, you are no longer a child, and I am no longer a young girl. We both understand what this is about, and we can consider all the consequences of our actions. Now that you have decided to declare your love to me today, I naturally assume that you want to marry me."

He hadn't expected such a clear statement, and he replied dumbly:

"Of course."

"Have you spoken to your father and mother about this?"

"No. I wanted to know if you would agree first."

She extended her still wet hand to him, he quickly clasped his hand on hers, and she said:

"As for me, I am very willing. I believe that you are kind and sincere. But you must remember that I do not want to make your parents unhappy."

"Ah! Do you think my mother hasn't anticipated this? If she didn't want us to get married, would she love you as much as she does now?"

"That's true. I am a little worried about her intentions."

Relationship Between Silver Prices and Chinese Price Levels

(Continued from the previous installment) By Lewis, translated by Zhang Luluan

If we take 1910 to 1914 as the base period, then the quantity of goods imported into China was 41.2 in 1887 and 186.8 in 1930, seemingly continuously increasing. However, on the other hand, the decline in the purchasing power of silver in the decade from 1923 to 1931 was unprecedented in history. Yet, China's population increased particularly rapidly. Since May 1931, China's price levels began to decline, and the index of imported goods also decreased from 186.8 to 160.8. In 1932, it was only 136.0. It can be seen that the magnitude of China's purchasing power is inversely proportional to the level of silver prices. However, the index for the three northeastern provinces in 1932 is only a rough estimate.

In gold standard countries, prices began to decline from 1929, and commerce gradually declined invisibly. Whether foreign goods or domestically produced items, transactions were extremely sluggish. In China, low prices have already caused farmers to experience acute hardship. If the decline continues, the current wage rates will inevitably be unsustainable, unemployment will increase, and various cooperative companies and banks will also suffer. Currently, the prices of agricultural products have made it difficult for farmers to repay debts and pay taxes. Since China is an agricultural country, when prices fall, rural prices are often worse than others. Therefore, the devastation of rural economies due to price declines in China is greater than in cities, which is completely different from the situation in other countries. Therefore, reducing the purchasing power of foreign goods in China is only one of the smallest manifestations of the various difficulties and dangers that arise after the increase in silver prices. (To be continued)

The Third Estimate of National Cotton Production in the 22nd Year

The China Cotton Industry Statistics Association announced the third estimate of national cotton production in the 22nd year at 5:00 PM on December 15, 22nd year as follows:

Cotton field area 40,453,953 mu

Ginned cotton production 9,621,240 dan

Abandoned field area 617,398 mu

The above estimates are based on (1) reports from eleven provinces including Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, as well as the two cities of Shanghai and Tianjin, (2) based on the cotton crop conditions before December 10, (3) the losses caused by disasters suffered by the cotton crop in various provinces before December 10 have been calculated, (4) the cotton field is in Chinese mu, and the cotton production is in dan (100 jin per dan).

The first, second, and third estimates of this year, the cotton field production in previous years, and the three estimates published annually in the past two years are compared below.

Dan Cotton Field Area (mu) Ginned Cotton Production (dan)

Year 8 33,037,881 9,028,390

Year 9 28,327,297 6,750,403

Year 10 28,216,168 5,429,220

Year 11 33,464,595 8,310,355

Year 12 29,554,053 7,144,642

Year 13 28,771,577 7,808,882

Year 14 28,121,027 7,534,351

Year 15 27,349,727 6,243,585

Year 16 27,610,276 6,872,108

Year 17 31,926,311 8,839,274

Year 18 33,811,255 7,587,021

Year 19 37,593,012 8,809,567

Year 20 First Estimate 35,468,352 6,793,241

Second Estimate 34,182,747 6,460,641

Final Revision 31,637,779 6,399,780

Year 21 First Estimate 37,086,775 10,829,162

Second Estimate 37,079,835 8,094,863

Final Revision 37,099,800 8,105,637

Year 22 First Estimate 39,157,446 10,734,451

Second Estimate 39,684,369 9,838,286

Third Estimate 40,453,953 9,621,240

The cotton field areas of various provinces this year have increased in Hebei, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, and Jiangsu, especially in Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Hubei, and Jiangsu. Planting cotton along the Pinghan railway in Hebei is developing, especially with foreign cotton. In recent years, Shanxi has seen a revival in cotton production due to its relative stability. Henan and Shaanxi have seen less warfare, and with cheap grain prices, cotton fields have increased. Jiangsu and Hubei have been recovering rapidly in recent years since the great flood of the 20th year greatly reduced cotton fields. Other provinces are also progressing year by year. Therefore, the total amount of cotton fields has been progressing with time over the past few years. This year, the rainfall between spring and summer in the north was abundant, and cotton crops were able to be planted and stabilized in time. This is a major reason for the surge in cotton fields in the northern provinces this year. However, Shandong has decreased slightly, and many fields were flooded in the autumn due to the Yellow River flood. Fortunately, the water receded quickly, and there was no total crop failure. Therefore, the national cotton field area this year reached 39.15 million mu in the first estimate. Because the first survey this year was earlier, the second increased to 39.68 million mu. This estimate exceeds 40 million mu, the highest figure in the last 15 years. Therefore, in terms of the national cotton field area, it can be said to be progress. This estimate can be regarded as the final actual amount, estimated at 9,621,240 dan, which is an increase of 1,515,603 dan compared to the 21st year, and an increase of 3,221,460 dan compared to the 20th year. The amount of production is not only unprecedented in recent years, but also the largest production number since the eighth year of the Republic. However, the increase in cotton production is not due to the abundance of the harvest, but to the increase in the cotton field area. After all, the cotton field this year is also the highest number in the post-Republic era. In terms of harvest, it is only a medium harvest. (The increase in cotton fields is mainly in the north because the chaos of soldiers and bandits has subsided slightly, and farmers are somewhat safe, coupled with good weather and sufficient rainfall, so the cotton fields have increased.) The average yield per mu in the first estimate was 27.2 jin, which was the largest number since the eighth year of the Republic. Therefore, at that time, there was hope for a bumper cotton harvest this year. By the second estimate, it had decreased to 24.8 jin. This estimate is further reduced to 23.8 jin, which is 2 jin higher than the final actual harvest of 21.8 jin in the 21st year, and is equal to the average number of 23.8 jin for the fourteen years since the eighth year of the Republic (23.8 jin per mu for the total number of fourteen years).

Education News: Director Mallerk of the Foreign Danish International Folk High School Will Visit China, Passing Through Our Country to Travel to the United States, and Will Give Lectures in Shanghai and Wuxi

Dr. Mallerk, the director of the Danish International Folk High School, is well-versed in various social legislation systems and has a deep understanding of rural improvement, which is closely related to China's current situation, and can promote adult education in rural society. Recently, Mr. Mallerk plans to travel to the United States and Canada via the East, passing through India and China. He is expected to arrive in Hong Kong on January 6 next year. After a short rest in Hong Kong, he will go to Guangzhou to give a lecture. From about January 14 to 24, he will go to Shanghai, Wuxi, and Nanjing, and then go to Jinan, Linping, Tianjin, Beiping, and Dingxian to give lectures. He will be in China for about five weeks. As for Mr. Mallerk's scheduled topics, 1. The prosperity of Danish folk high schools and rural society, 2. Mr. Grongeweg, the pioneer of Northern Europe, 3. Grongeweg and Danish folk high schools, 4. Denmark's social legislation system, 5. The International Folk High School, 6. Various views of various ethnic groups on education, 7. The nationality of Northern Europeans and Germans, 8. Denmark's cooperative movement and land policy. Ms. Yu Qingtang of the Wuxi Provincial Folk Education College has received the news and is preparing to welcome and entertain him at that time.

Minister of Education's Higher Education Director Shen Pengfei Discusses Academic Degrees: Degrees Obtained Abroad Cannot Be Considered Chinese Degrees

The Riri News Agency reports that recently, the educational authorities, considering that our country's academic degrees are based on those obtained abroad, which greatly diminishes the dignity of an independent nation, are planning to create our own degree system. Doctoral, master's, and bachelor's degrees will be determined through examinations. After this news was released, all parties paid close attention. A reporter from the Riri News Agency in Beijing specifically visited Shen Pengfei, Director of Higher Education at the Ministry of Education, to inquire about the content of the academic degree law. According to Shen, the drafting of the academic degree law did not begin today. Four or five years ago, when Mr. Cai (Yuanpei) and Mr. Jiang (Menglin) were ministers, they, along with Mr. Dai (Jitao), President of the Examination Yuan, drafted the principles of academic degrees and sent them to the Legislative Yuan for drafting. However, it has not been completed. After Mr. Zhu (Jiahua) became Minister of Education, he also had this intention. When Minister Wang (Shijie) took office, he inherited Mr. Zhu's intentions and discussed the matter with President Dai of the Examination Yuan. President Dai also eagerly wanted to complete this task. Currently, the draft academic degree law proposed by the Ministry of Education has been reviewed by the Examination Committee and sent to the Central Administrative Regulations Committee for discussion. After the discussion, it will be sent to the Legislative Yuan for drafting. The content cannot be disclosed because the discussion is not yet complete, but there are certain points that can be reported in advance: (1) Doctoral, master's, and bachelor's degrees obtained abroad cannot be considered Chinese doctoral, master's, and bachelor's degrees because the standards of degrees obtained abroad are not uniform. (2) Anyone who wants to obtain a doctoral, master's, or bachelor's degree must pass a rigorous examination by the government. It is stipulated that examinations will be held once every few years, and the number of candidates per examination will be limited to ten. Whether graduates of domestic national universities or private universities approved by the Ministry of Education can immediately obtain a bachelor's degree depends on the regulations of the academic degree law. It is still difficult to predict when the examinations will begin. In short, our country is an independent nation in the world, and it is necessary to have the freedom to grant academic degrees. This measure can not only maintain the dignity of the nation but also prevent domestic scholars from feeling suppressed. We sincerely hope that it will be implemented as soon as possible.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Sends Supervisors of Provincial Institutions Abroad for Observation

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education announced a general outline for selecting and sending supervisors of provincial educational institutions abroad for observation, stating: 1. For the purpose of improving education in the province, the Department of Education may select and send supervisors of provincial educational institutions abroad for observation. 2. Overseas observation is divided into the following two types: A. Domestic observation; B. Overseas observation. 3. The number of people dispatched for domestic and overseas observation each time will be allocated according to the following proportions: General Education: 2 domestic, 2 overseas; Normal Education: 1 domestic, 1 overseas; Rural Normal Education: 1 domestic, 1 overseas; Vocational Education: 1 domestic, 1 overseas; Primary Education: 2 domestic, 2 overseas; Social Education Institutions: 1 domestic, 1 overseas. 4. Domestic and overseas observations may be dispatched in installments. 5. The matters and locations for observation will be determined temporarily by the Department of Education. 6. The observation period is limited to a maximum of one month for domestic and a maximum of two months for overseas. 7. The observation travel expenses are limited to 150 yuan per person for domestic and 500 yuan per person for overseas, which will be paid from the educational expenses. 8. Supervisors of provincial educational institutions who have served for more than one year and have outstanding achievements may be selected and sent by the Department of Education. 9. After completing the observation, the observer should submit a detailed report on the observations and provide opinions on improving education in the province for consideration. 10. This general outline will be announced and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education.

The Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee held its fourth standing committee meeting at the Shanghai Joint Entertainment Club in the Silk Industry Building on Sanma Road at 4:00 PM yesterday to discuss matters such as the organization of the Shanghai Children's Year Committee (next year). Resolutions of Various Cases

After the customary formalities, the chairman reported on the location of the nursery, the start-up costs, and the progress of the work. Then, the discussion of the organizational outline of the Shanghai Children's Year Committee began. (1) The case of the organizational outline of the Shanghai Children's Year Committee was (resolved) amended and approved. (2) The case of approving the list of members of the Shanghai Children's Year Committee was (resolved) amended and approved. (3) The case of approving the publicity measures for Children's Year was (resolved) (1) Publish a regular periodical (in cooperation with the Children's Morning Post), (2) Major newspapers will publish special issues on New Year's Day, Children's Day, and other festivals, (3) Print the Shanghai Children's Year Association President's Awards, (4) For the opening of Shanghai Children's Year, invite Mayor Wu to host children from the city and other countries in the new city government building and visit the performances, (5) Stipulate the dates and frequency of children's films in various cinemas. (4) The case of approving the funding measures for Children's Year was (resolved) 1. Request the municipal government to allocate monthly regular expenses to the Shanghai Children's Year Committee, 2. Request subsidies from the Children's Welfare Committee, the China Child Welfare Association, and other children's welfare organizations, 3. The ad hoc expenses will be the responsibility of the association's economic group to raise. (5) The case of approving the Children's Year projects was (resolved) 1. Contact the city's film industry to produce children's films, 2. Take in homeless children, 3. Prohibit child betrothal, 4. Build and open children's parks in the southern city, the northern city, and Jiangwan, 5. Hold children's education broadcasts, 6. Publish children's newspapers, 7. Strictly prohibit abuse, trafficking, and oppression of children, 8. Promote children's savings, 9. Reward children's various creations, 10. Promote children's health check-ups.

Committee Organization

The Shanghai Children's Year Committee is divided into two departments: the General Affairs Department and the Project Department. The General Affairs Department is divided into three groups: (1) Standing Committee Group, (2) Publicity Group, (3) Economic Group. The Project Department is divided into six groups: (1) Children's National Products Group, (2) Children's Culture Group, (3) Children's Health Group, (4) Children's Service Group, (5) Children's Entertainment Group, (6) Children's Relief Group.

Basketball Quarter-Final Results

Jinling Eliminates Soochow: The Jinling vs. Soochow basketball quarter-final took place yesterday at 10 a.m. Jinling played bravely and strategically and proved to be a strong team. Soochow, though outstanding in the Wu region, was ultimately defeated. After the opening, Lin Jianxue scored one point because Hou Mulin committed a foul. Hou Mulin atoned for his fault, and Soochow took the lead with a score of 2-0. Zhu Peifeng committed another foul, and Gong Desheng scored twice, giving Jinling a 3-2 lead. Hou Mulin made a successful long shot, and Soochow regained the lead with 4-3. Lin Heipi got excited and made a long shot that missed, but he followed up with a close-range shot, successfully scoring twice. Jinling took a 7-4 lead, and Soochow requested a time-out, but it had no effect. Lin Heipi scored again, and Jinling's score steadily increased. Although Zhou Bencai of Soochow made some amazing shots, it was not enough to help. At the end of the first half, Jinling won by 19 to 9, leading by ten points. In the second half, Soochow suddenly changed its strategy. Hou Mulin launched an attack from the center, which proved effective. Zhou Bencai lurked on the left and scored even more points. Although Lin Mopi of Jinling scored twice, the score gradually narrowed. Zhu Peifeng of Soochow had a moment of inspiration and made a long shot that went over the beam and straight into the net, making the score 18-23. Soochow was only five points behind. The Jinling players looked at each other in dismay and requested a time-out to slightly diminish the opponent's momentum. When the game resumed, Jinling suddenly became active, and Heipi was particularly commendable. Soochow's energy had waned, and they only relied on long shots. Jinling then won the quarter-final spot with a score of 41-28.

In less than five minutes, center Chen Zheng'en took a long shot from 20 yards away from the goal. The goalkeeper of Soochow, Liu Erzhan, overreached and ended up in the net. Zhou Bencai's corner kick landed perfectly, and Ma Taiyuan and others scored a goal. Taowu won with a score of 2-0. Soochow had the opportunity to counterattack, and the students strongly supported them. Taowu was surrounded on all sides. Guo Zhihua scored a goal, and Taowu won the first half with a score of 2-1. Not long after the start of the second half, Chen Zheng'en committed a foul outside the penalty area. Guo Zhihua took the penalty kick and scored another goal, making the score 2-2. The forwards of Taowu were unwilling to be outdone. Left winger Yan Shengquan dribbled past Gu Dechang, raised his right foot, and shot the ball quickly and accurately. Liu Kouzhan of Soochow stared blankly. Taowu won again with a score of 3-2. Chen Zheng'en picked up the ball, and Xu Yishan scored a goal. Taowu then won with a score of 4-2 and won the consolation quarter-final spot.

Summary of Changes to the 1933-1934 Basketball Rules

Announced by the National Amateur Athletic Federation

There are very few changes to the rules this season, which will not have much impact on the game. The ten-second and three-second rules have been successfully implemented. The important points of the changes are listed below for reference. Once the new rule book is received, it will be translated and officially announced.

(1) Each player can participate in the game three times in the same match, except for those who are disqualified, that is, once they leave the field, they can re-enter the game twice.

(2) After a successful shot or free throw, the referee does not need to blow the whistle to signal.

(3) After a team has passed the ball to the frontcourt, the ball is only allowed to be passed back to the backcourt once by the player who first touches the ball after four situations: (a) after shooting the basket, (b) after a jump ball, (c) after the ball goes out of bounds, and (d) after the ball is taken by the opponent and then regained.

(4) The right to throw the ball out of bounds belongs to the team in the frontcourt area, then the referee should first obtain the ball before continuing the game.

Spring and Autumn

Wu Qu'an's Views on Studying Literature

— Yan Qiao

Mr. Qu'an is a modern expert in lyrics and music, has in-depth research in Chinese literature, and is also an old professor. He was very young when he first taught at Soochow University, and now he has more than 30 years of teaching experience. The day before yesterday, he came to the Literary Society of Soochow University to give a lecture. Because I had some things to do, I could not stay until the end, and only heard the first section of his "Views on Studying Literature," which was about antithesis. He said that antithesis is a habit of people. For example, when saying a sentence, one must cite an example. If that is not enough, add another one. This is the origin of antithesis.

Later, my friend told me that there were three more sections below. The second section was about the Book of Rites, saying that after reading a book, one should write down one's心得（心得 means: what one learned, thought, or felt）The third section was about reading articles, saying that articles must be read, and must be read with enthusiasm. If you don't read, you won't be familiar with it. To be enthusiastic, you must read it. Most people don't read now, so they can't be called scholars, but only book readers. The fourth section was about recognizing characters, saying that mispronounced words are very jarring and make people feel that the person is uneducated. Although these four points are clichés, they are very practical, unlike those speakers who talk about the sea and the sky, only winning applause from the audience, and after counting, there is nothing to be gained.

I think the fourth section is the most meaningful, and the social habits are even more ridiculous. For example, the character 廬 (Lú) in Mount Lu is clearly pronounced Lǘ, but people in Shanghai insist on pronouncing it as Lú. The character 龔 (Gōng) in Gong Ding'an is clearly pronounced Gōng, but people in Suzhou insist on pronouncing it as the level tone of the character 炯 (Jiǒng). However, comparatively speaking, people in Shanghai mispronounce more words, such as the character 樂 (Yuè) in military band, which is pronounced as Luò. The character 娛 (Yú) in entertainment is pronounced as Wù. Previously, there was a restaurant called Yihong Restaurant, and they pronounced the character 倚 (Yǐ) as the character 奇 (Qí), but no one called the novelist Bi Yihong as Qi Hong.

What is even more inconceivable is that the five characters 美麗川菜館 (Měilì Chuāncài Guǎn, Beautiful Sichuan Restaurant) are divided into two parts: 美麗川 (Měilì Chuān, Beautiful Sichuan) and 菜館 (càiguǎn, Restaurant).

Anecdotes of International Diplomacy

— Xiao Ying

As I have heard: In the front and behind the scenes of diplomacy, there have been some interesting anecdotes. Some were ignored by people at the time, and some were unknown to the outside world. Although they are not of great importance, they are still interesting to talk about afterwards. I have selected them here to bring a smile to your face.

During the September 18th Incident, it is said that our Ministry of Foreign Affairs had difficulty obtaining accurate information for a while, so when foreign news agency reporters went to inquire about the news, they did not have a concrete answer.

When the situation in the Far East was tense, the State Department in Washington became the center of international politics. Once, our Minister Shih Shih-hsuan was meeting with Stimson when the Japanese Ambassador Debuchi Katsu suddenly arrived uninvited. The clever American diplomatic doorman, on the one hand, invited Debuchi to another room, and on the other hand, took Shih's hat and coat and waited by the door to avoid the trouble of the diplomatic representatives of the two countries meeting.

When the League of Nations discussed the Northeast issue, the Japanese representative Yoshizawa suddenly announced that he would speak in Japanese. For a time, newspapers spread that Mr. Yoshizawa was not good at French; but according to those familiar with the inside story, Mr. Yoshizawa was not ignorant of French, and the reason why he relied on a translator was to prepare a place to deny it if there were any modifications in the prepared speech.

British diplomacy is known for its gentlemanly attitude; however, when The Hague discussed the German reparations issue, Snowden used extremely stupid words to scold the French representative, because this man was not a diplomatic talent and the situation was urgent, so he spoke without thinking.

Brief Thoughts

— He Shan

Sugar-fried chestnuts; of course, they are delicious, and I love to eat them too.

Early this morning, about nine o'clock? Two modern ladies got on the streetcar. As soon as they sat down, they opened a paper bag of sugar-fried chestnuts and started eating them. Using their bright red fingernails, they peeled the chestnut shells and put them into their bloody mouths one by one. They ate, talked, and laughed. Just as they were happily eating, an old foreign lady next to them immediately put on a straight face and said: "This is First Class. Please Don't!" The two ladies smiled cheekily and replied in broken English, "All Right!" and immediately put away the paper bag, still talking and laughing nonchalantly. When the streetcar arrived at the Bund, the old foreign lady got off, and the two ladies started eating again, scattering chestnut shells all over the floor.

This small, accidental event raised several questions in my mind: First, if these two ladies were foreign misses, I wonder if the old foreign lady would have interfered in the same way. Second, the common advertisements on the streetcar are nothing more than prohibitions on spitting, smoking, and pulling the bell, as well as several wooden signs on rules about preventing theft and checking monthly tickets, but I have never seen a notice prohibiting eating sugar-fried chestnuts. I don't know which rule this old lady relied on to have the right to interfere. Third, the old lady said this was first class, but I don't know what the difference between first class and third class is besides the different fares.

But we can't blame others too much, or blame ourselves too little. Although everyone loves to eat sugar-fried chestnuts, for these two ladies to eat sugar-fried chestnuts early in the morning, after already having eaten breakfast (which they probably already had), is probably not hygienic. Even if they wanted to eat, why did they have to eat them on the streetcar? After being advised not to eat, why did they make such an ugly scene after the old lady left? It's really incomprehensible.

Littering fruit shells on the streetcar is fundamentally a problem of public morality. To be honest, the public morality of our esteemed countrymen is not very good. It is not unreasonable for the old foreign lady to interfere with the Chinese ladies eating sugar-fried chestnuts, but to treat them with harsh words and a stern expression in international etiquette seems unreasonable, right?

My friend Xiao Yue has spent much effort and care on detective novels. He has racked his brains, thought deeply, and wrote diligently, never giving up until recently, such as the collection of Huo Sang Detective Cases, sequel, a huge book. Huo Sang, in fact, does not exist as a person, just like the English writer Conan Doyle and Sherlock Holmes. Mr. Cheng is extremely patriotic, and has always taken the task of elaborating the essence of Chinese culture through science as his duty, so whenever he creates something, he always touches on the common knowledge of physical and chemical evolution, and the interconnection of the main lines is like tasting a persimmon, which contains a long aftertaste, quite unlike the criticism of adding twists and turns. This can be said to be its greatest strength.

The novel "Jiangnan Yan" is Mr. He's debut work, which was published in the Xianshi Amusement Park Daily, and there is a separate edition. However, the book is already out of print in the market. The book describes "Jiangnan Yan" raising funds for a poor people's orphanage, so he borrowed the family's secret "Cat's Eye" as collateral from a local tycoon. The tycoon's daughter, because of her father's illness, personally went to Huo Sang to ask him to keep it in custody on her behalf. Huo believed that Yan's intelligence was no less than his, so he deliberately set up various traps to avoid miscalculation. And "Jiangnan Yan" was very powerful and never entered Huo's trap. The two heroes used their intelligence, which was quite painstaking. In addition, there were the tender emotions of children, villains pretending to collect money, and the assistant's recklessness, being tricked, etc., which added beautiful materials to the warm and tense atmosphere, making readers forget their fatigue. One cannot reach this point without a quick mind and a clear pen.

In recent years, the style of movies has gradually moved towards the right track, and detective works can really help education. Therefore, the film company should choose the best and make more of them. My friend Youlian Company, through my introduction, took the novel "Jiangnan Yan" and adapted it into a film drama. This film is already being released to introduce it to those who love to read Mr. Cheng's works and love film art.

Mr. Jiang said: "Please come into the house and sit down." Old man Zhao chuckled and walked into the house. He no longer had his dry tobacco pipe in his hand, and he kept rubbing his palms together. When she saw Old man Zhao enter, she stood up, called out in a low voice "Old Master," and stood by the door without moving. Old man Zhao said: "I heard that you caught a cold, are you still not well?" Old man Zhao was just about to sit down on a chair, when he heard these words, he stood up again, touched his beard with his left hand, and pointed at Gui Zhi with his right index finger, laughing: "It's all because of your affairs that I'm so happy. When your mother said to call Zi Qiang back for the wedding, I was overjoyed and couldn't help but clap my hands and shout 'Good!' This dry tobacco pipe followed the commotion and also stomped its foot on the ground. It didn't matter that it stomped its foot, but it made a somersault and broke the mouthpiece. Breaking it is fine, consider it helping me out." Mr. Jiang laughed: "Old Master is too frugal, how much money can you spend on smoking dry tobacco in a month? You still have to take this opportunity to forget smoking." Old man Zhao reached into his pocket, took out a box of cigarettes, held it up, and said with a smile: "I can't bear to buy cigarettes, the money for a box of cigarettes can at least be used to smoke dry tobacco for six or seven days. But since the dry tobacco pipe is broken, I'll take the opportunity to buy two boxes and smoke them. These are Beauty brand, Madam, would you like to smoke one?" Mr. Jiang couldn't help but laugh and say: "This is really the dry tobacco pipe's mouthpiece helping you out, since the dry tobacco pipe's mouthpiece is broken, you're smoking Beauty brand cigarettes." Old man Zhao laughed and said: "Dear lady, you can count that as scolding me, an old antique like me, what's there to talk about beauty or not beauty, I'm just picking a new type of cigarette to smoke and try it out." Radio Weekly

The Latest Automatic Frequency Adjustment Method

— Ming Xiang

Ordinary radios have three adjustment knobs: volume control, tone control, and the most important frequency adjustment. The first two have already had automatic control methods invented. This journal has previously written about it, but only the most important frequency adjustment has not been heard of being able to use automatic methods.

Frequency adjustment of radios is done in the input circuit of each stage (except the sound frequency amplification stage), using an inductor and a capacitor to form an adjustment circuit. Changing the capacitance of this capacitor allows the intrinsic frequency of the circuit to resonate with the frequency of the radio waves emitted by a certain station, and then the signal from that station can be received.

Recently, a British radio magazine published a very interesting automatic frequency adjustment circuit. This circuit can resonate with radio waves of any external frequency without adjustment. The component that achieves this automatic adjustment goal is still the soul of radio, the vacuum tube.

Anyone with some radio knowledge probably knows that there is a certain static capacitance between each electrode inside a vacuum tube. A few years ago, scientist Miller discovered that this capacitance is not the same when the vacuum tube is heated and cooled. Not only that, but the amount of its change depends entirely on the vacuum tube output and the type of circuit used. In other words, the capacitance between the filament and the grid of a vacuum tube can be changed due to the effective total impedance of its output circuit.

If an inductor is connected in the screen circuit of a vacuum tube, the total impedance of the screen circuit must automatically increase as the frequency increases, thus affecting the capacitance between the grid and the filament. Therefore, we can design an inductive output circuit so that the capacitance between the grid and the filament automatically increases at long wavelengths and automatically decreases at short wavelengths, thus completing the automatic adjustment goal.

The circuit is shown in the figure. The input circuit of the screen grid amplifier tube does not need to be adjusted, but the grid and filament of a triode are connected in parallel with the coil L1 to replace the usual variable capacitor. Its screen is connected to the positive pole of the B battery through a load inductor Z. If the frequency of the external signal changes, the effective inductance of Z in the screen circuit of the automatic adjustment tube also changes, thus the capacitance between the grid and the filament also automatically changes, still maintaining its resonant state.

Of course, a pre-selector must be passed before this type of circuit, otherwise radio waves of any frequency will resonate at the same time, and the sound emitted by the radio will inevitably be chaotic and impossible to select and distinguish.

How a Direct Current Uses a Transformer

— Shi Huayu

Don't we often say that direct current can't use a transformer? Why can't it? Isn't the primary coil of a low-frequency transformer usually connected in series with the plate circuit of a detector tube? Isn't the detector tube plate current pure direct current? Why can it use a transformer? It turns out that induced current is generated because the conductor is moving in a magnetic field, or the magnetic lines of force passing through the coil change. The so-called direct current output of the detector tube plate circuit is actually a fluctuating direct current. After passing through the primary coil of a low-frequency transformer, it generates changing magnetic lines of force. These changing magnetic lines of force pass through the secondary coil, so an induced current is generated in the secondary coil. In short, as long as the magnetic lines of force passing through the secondary can change, an induced current can be generated. The one that causes these magnetic lines of force to change can be alternating current or pulsating direct current, both are fine. A stable battery current can also be used if it is interrupted. Now, if we apply a current (Break) to the primary of the transformer, an induced current will be generated in the secondary. If the number of turns of the secondary and primary coils are in a certain ratio, then the voltage of the primary and secondary will also be in a certain ratio, thus completing the purpose of boosting or reducing the voltage. Now that we understand the above principle, direct current can also use a transformer to boost or reduce its voltage.

An ordinary alternating current radio's power transformer can be slightly modified to be used for direct current power. As shown in the figure, T is the power transformer. M is an electromagnet, and Q is a steel sheet. Its installation is exactly the same as a doorbell, but the higher the vibration frequency of Q, the more advantageous it is. When QD is cut off, that is, when they are not in contact, the secondary S will generate current. The capacitor has a larger capacity, about between 2Mfd and M8fd. Because when the primary circuit is cut off at point QD, due to the self-induction of the primary, sparks must occur between QD, thus forming an oscillator. Therefore, the opening and closing of the primary circuit is affected, and the cutoff is delayed, and high electromotive force cannot be generated. If a C capacitor is added, the self-induced current flows into the capacitor, no sparks are generated between QD, and rapid cutoff can be obtained to generate high electromotive force. As for the thickness of the coil wound on M, it should be the same as the primary to minimize losses.

Dual-Tone Loudspeaker

— Chun

Because ordinary components, even the most precise speakers, cannot achieve the goal of making the music broadcast on the radio station received in the radio fully clear, people began to try to use a dual-tone loudspeaker device. I found several reference materials in RadioCraft, adopted the most complete one, and experimented several times. The sound received is very clear, both the subtle and the most grand parts. I think this dual-tone loudspeaker has satisfied my desire. This method is also very simple and easy to try. All it costs is two transformers, two capacitors, and one more speaker. Two output vacuum tubes are also required. Now, let's take the simplest circuit to illustrate. On any radio, you can connect two speakers in this way to become dual-tone.

As for the installation, the styles of the two speakers are different. The larger the mouth of the speaker, the clearer the low-frequency sound is emitted. Conversely, the smaller the mouth of the speaker, the clearer the high-frequency sound is emitted. Therefore, in the installation of a dual-tone loudspeaker, one speaker should use a narrow diameter, and the other should use a large diameter. It is best to use push-pull transformers to leave room for tuning the scales and compensate for the deficiency of capacitors. The capacitors I personally use have seventeen pieces, and 0.0025 is generally used as the standard. If there is noise in the speaker, you can connect the center tap of the push-pull transformer (primary middle) to the positive terminal of the B battery. But if the installation is proper, it is not necessary to connect it. This can only be determined based on the results of experiments, and it cannot be fixed whether it needs to be connected or not.

The advantage of this dual-tone loudspeaker is that it does not distort the original sound. You might as well try it.

Improvement of Using Low-Frequency Transformers to Replace Filter Chokes

— KMK

Generally, amateur radio researchers all consider economic aspects. For example, in alternating current radios, most researchers use low-frequency transformers to replace the filter chokes in the rectifier section. Although this is convenient and economical, it has a shortcoming, that is, the alternating current sound cannot be completely filtered out, which is a pity. Because the current is input from point F, and suddenly changes its direction of flow between GP, resulting in an unstable direct current output from point B. At this time, an annoying alternating current sound will occur in the radio. When there are the above-mentioned disadvantages, a 2Mfd fixed capacitor can be connected between GP and the negative terminal (as shown in the figure) to remedy the situation.

Small Experiences

— RF

Hard Rubber Dislikes Sunlight

Products made of hard rubber should not be exposed to sunlight. Because over time, the power of sunlight can cause a kind of decomposition reaction in hard rubber, causing a part of the sulfur in the hard rubber to form a thin layer and remain on its surface, resulting in the disadvantage of leakage current and losing its insulation effect. Therefore, hard rubber used for high-voltage insulation must pay attention to this point. If it can be replaced with bakelite material, it is more appropriate.

Winding of Non-Inductive Resistors

The resistance of resistors wound with resistance wire often produces back electromotive force due to the effect of induction. To avoid this disadvantage, the winding method should use a non-inductive one. The method is as follows: A. Fold the wire at the midpoint of its entire length so that the two ends meet, and then wind this double-stranded wire in the usual way. B. Divide the wire into several layers and wind them in opposite directions on each layer. (That is, the first layer is opposite to the second layer, and the second layer is opposite to the third layer.)

Polarity Test Paper

When using direct current, if you cannot determine the positive and negative poles, you can distinguish them with polarity test paper. Manufacturing method: Take one gram of phenolphthalein, dissolve it in a small amount of alcohol. Take a pinch of salt and dissolve it in a cup of water. Then mix the two liquids, take Chinese paper and cut it into small strips, wet them with this solution, and then dry them in the shade to form the test paper. Usage: Take a strip of this paper and wet it with water. Separate the two poles of the electricity slightly and touch them to the paper. The electrode that emits bright red color near it is the negative pole. The principle: Because the current flows through the salt solution, light sodium hydroxide is generated at the negative pole due to electrolysis. Light sodium hydroxide is an alkaline substance, so it reacts with phenolphthalein to emit red color. (Note: Phenolphthalein is sold in instrument stores and Western pharmacies.)

Radio Knowledge

— Huang Jiancun

(Twenty-one) Overview of Vacuum Tubes (5)

(8) Quick-heating AC tube (Quickbeatertype): AC tubes are most popular with side-heated ones because they are convenient, and many people like to use them. However, there is a disadvantage, that is, the heat emitted from the heating part (Hoater) must be conducted to the cathode through an insulator, so its starting work is delayed. To remedy this shortcoming, small holes are opened in the insulator so that it can supply heat by radiation. Although this design can speed up the starting work of the vacuum tube, on the other hand, the higher the quick-heating property, the easier the AC sound is to occur. Therefore, the manufacturer must appropriately select the compromise point between the two so as not to lose sight of the other. At present, the vacuum tube with relatively quick-heating property is the Philips brand, and its starting work time is usually between ten and thirty seconds.

(9) Pentode for high frequency: Because the tetrode has secondary electron emission, the plate voltage and plate current cannot be changed greatly. This state has been described. To make the plate voltage change greatly, it is necessary to increase the value of the plate voltage. It is quite easy to increase the plate voltage for AC radios or fixed battery radios; however, for mobile or car radios, it is hoped that the number of batteries will be reduced as much as possible, so the plate voltage cannot be increased. So the pentode appeared to solve this kind of difficulty, and it was initially limited to low frequency use. Recently, various pentodes for high frequency have also been produced one after another. For example, the RCA No. 239 tube can be used for radios in a car, and the RCA No. 34 tube can be used for DC portable radios. They can be used for amplification at high frequency and intermediate frequency, as well as the first detection of non-grid heterodyne, but it is impossible to use them for ordinary plate detection.

The so-called new tubes No. 57 and No. 58 produced in the past year are AC versions of pentodes for high frequency. Their filament voltages are all 2.5 volts, and their plate voltages are even increased to 250 volts, which is unprecedented, commonly known as AC 2.5 volt tubes.

The Lifeline of the Electrical World

— Lü Bing

It is said that the island country to the east divides demarcation lines on the map, calling them "lifelines." The area they consider the first lifeline has long been made into a pseudo-country, and at the same time, about 15,000 kilometers of our country's communication lines have also been lost; but since the territory has been lost, these mere lines are not worth mentioning. We can only sigh with emotion about this! What is there to say! 丨丨 What is there to say!

The "lifeline" referred to by the Japanese is a euphemism for aggression. In fact, it has nothing to do with the survival of that country and cannot be regarded as necessary for life; however, the term "lifeline" is quite novel in terms of meaning. If it is applied to telecommunications, it is also quite accurate. After all, in the telecommunications business, "lines" occupy an important position. Whether it is wire telegraphy and telephone, or even radio, why don't they use sky-earth lines? They are scattered like stars, just like the nervous system of the human body. If telecommunications are considered to have vitality, then this kind of line that reaches all parts of the country can certainly be regarded as the "lifeline" of telecommunications traffic.

Since electrical wires are related to traffic, just as described above, similar to human life, then rectifying old lines is no different from prolonging the old life of telecommunications; constructing new lines is also no different from creating new life for telecommunications. Since it is related to life, it naturally cannot be ignored. Therefore, successive traffic authorities have spared no effort in the facilities and progress of lines. To mention recent events, whether it is Jinpu or Jinghu, they are all planning to rebuild or build new lines to connect long-distance telephones, and the original important trunk lines of Pinghan, Longhai, Huhan, Qinghu, Hanyu, and Jinpu are also successively repairing and replacing wooden poles on a large scale (wooden poles can be regarded as supporting objects for the lifeline) and sorting out the lines; in addition, in the bandit suppression areas and important areas, specialized personnel are also deployed to engage in line repair. It is because of this that telecommunications can maintain smooth operation; the hope for the life of telecommunications seems to lie here as well. It has been found that the machines installed in the bureau are as important as the lines. If electrical wires are regarded as "lifelines," then why can't machines be regarded as "vitality"; however, "a lifeline," vitality must ultimately rely on the application of a lifeline. I am only providing a strained interpretation, I hope you will not misunderstand the meaning of the words).

To go a step further, electrical wires are not only regarded as life in telecommunications traffic, but also ordinary people who do not care much about them usually feel full attention to the blockage of lines after turmoil; otherwise, since the Minbian Incident, the electric wires on the edge of Zhejiang have been obstructed all the way, how could it cause various rumors? Once restored, how could it make people feel a little settled? There is a relationship here. Although it is not direct, it can also indirectly infer the situation and fate. Who says it is not appropriate to call it a "lifeline"?

A View of the Telegraph Bureau, Past and Present

— Zhe Sheng

My country has been running the telegraph for more than 50 years. From being run by officials and merchants, to being supervised by officials and run by merchants, to being taken over by the state, due to the different nature, the change of the times, and the change of the environment, all systems and atmospheres have also gradually shifted and gradually changed the old view. Now I will list the points where we have felt the differences between the past and the present in recent years:

1. Business In the past, the telegraph bureau was similar to the Baojia Bureau and the Smuggling Bureau. Notices were posted on the wall, and a tiger plaque was hung on the door, which was like a government office. People who entered the bureau to send telegrams were like villagers paying land tax to the government office, bowing their heads and not daring to speak much. The officers and clerks in the bureau who received and sent telegrams sat arrogantly, as if they didn't see them. Receiving telegrams had to be done at their convenience, and scolding would follow if they didn't agree. The sender would retreat obediently and dare not argue. Today's telegraph bureau is different. The setting of the telegram receiving and sending office is like a store. The receiving and sending personnel are also mostly friendly and polite, and treat the telegram-sending public like a store treats customers. When there are inquiries, they will answer sincerely, and the change will be fair. Each bureau also has so-called business inspectors, who check all day long whether the messengers are delaying the delivery of telegrams or extorting translation fees, and also inquire about the opinions of the general public on the business of the telegraph bureau, so as to improve it at any time to meet the needs of the public. The telegraph bureau in the style of a government office in the past has now become a commercialized and public-oriented institution. In the old days, the price was increased according to the province and region, that is, a certain amount was added for each province. It was both cumbersome and expensive. Later, it was changed to two types: this province and another province. In recent years, it has been changed to a uniform price, which is the same in all provinces, which is much more convenient. The names and addresses of the recipients of Chinese telegrams are often as many as seven, eight, or more than ten characters, resulting in a telegram fee of several yuan, which the general public often finds too expensive. Since the implementation of the telegram registration method, only one registered character can be used to replace the name and address of the recipient. Recently, in busy cities, telephone numbers can be used to replace the address of the recipient, which is even more convenient. In addition, there are New Year's telegrams and social telegrams, which are inexpensive and without delay. There are many innovations in business.

2. Telegraph Service In the past, telegraph bureaus of all sizes transmitted telegrams with Morse telegraph machines regardless of the complexity of the telegraph service. The transmission rate was slow, and there was a risk of congestion in busy circuits. Now, all busy telegraph bureaus are equipped with Non-Weston express machines, and many have switched to duplex communication, that is, two bureaus can send telegrams simultaneously on the same line. The increase in the transmission rate of the Beijing and Shanghai bureaus, which have recently added new Kexin express machines, is more than double. In the past, telegraph operators valued official and military telegrams and ignored ordinary commercial telegrams (that is, private telegrams). Now, commercial telegrams and official and military telegrams are equally important. According to the author's investigation, telegrams between Shanghai and Hankou, Tianjin, Yantai, Qingdao, etc., although thousands of miles apart, can sometimes be received and sent by telephone at both ends, and the telegram can be received within ten minutes. The speed of transmission is surprising. Reduced price news telegrams are also sent as soon as they arrive without any delay. During the National Games held in the capital this time, the transmission of various sports news was extremely fast, which won a lot of praise from the media.

3. Personnel In the Qing Dynasty, the chief of the telegraph bureau (that is, the current director) was mostly a candidate official or a descendant of a noble family, with a full official air. Therefore, the entire bureau was also dyed into a bureaucracy, such as calling the director "Your Excellency" and calling the telegraph operators "Master". There were many levels within a bureau. The equipment in the bureau, except for the telegraph bureaus in a few busy cities, was very corrupt. Telegraph operators also had no proper entertainment in their spare time. Since the revolution, the bureaucratic habits have been gradually eliminated. The director is often a reformer, and the knowledge and hobbies of the telegraph operators are also very different from before. Each bureau has organizations such as book and newspaper clubs. In their spare time, they read books and newspapers to increase their knowledge, or exercise to cultivate their spirit. In the past ten years, publications in the telegraph industry have also sprung up like mushrooms after rain, competing to show new sprouts. Among them, such as Telecommunications Friend, Telecommunications Magazine, Current, Electric Bell, Telegraph Key, Electrical Engineering, and Electric Light, are all valuable publications in society. The football teams, table tennis teams, and Go teams organized by telecommunications colleagues also often compete with the outside world and achieve results. They are enthusiastic in contributing to the national salvation work, such as donating to the Northeast Volunteer Army, donating to the 19th Route Army, and donating to aviation construction. Therefore, today's telecommunications personnel have become prominent in society, unlike the obscurity of the past.

Simultaneous Telegraphy and Telephony

— Wang Dachun

In the same electric wire circuit, the method of installing telegraph and telephone for simultaneous communication is called Simultaneous Telegraphy and Telephony. This simultaneous communication method is further divided into two types: one is a Simplex Circuit, that is, only one telegraph circuit is installed in one telephone circuit. One is a Composite Cfrcuit, in which two telegraph circuits are installed in one telephone circuit. In our country, the places where the simultaneous telegraphy and telephony method is applied to long-distance telephone lines are not common. In the past, the long-distance telephone circuit between Zhenjiang and Yangzhou used two telegraph working lines to form a circuit. Both parties talked and sent telegrams, and the results were very good. The application has also been for many years. Later, the underwater cable crossing the Yangtze River was broken by the anchors of ships and was lost and could not be repaired. This communication method has been abandoned for a long time. It is now heard that the Ministry of Communications is planning to set up long-distance telephones along the Beijing-Shanghai Highway, and there is also a proposal to install a simultaneous telegraphy and telephony method. I will not hesitate to talk about its outline, which is expected to be welcomed by the readers.

The principle of a single-circuit is actually the same as the principle of a phantom circuit, as shown in Figure A: R and R1 are telegraph machines. C and C1 are condensers, whose volume is usually 2m·f·oT and T1 are telephones. L and L1 are long-distance telephone lines. is a Retardation Coil. The resistance of this plug flow line is usually 50 ohms. Its connection method is connected from the telegraph machine, like the extension of two arms, and the telephone and the external line are connected in parallel, so that the telephone at both ends is connected into a loop. The resistance of these two arms is usually adjusted to a balanced state. In this way, when the telegraph machine is communicating, the potential caused in the telephone line at the same time is equal. Therefore, the communication current flowing through the telephone line does not flow into the telephone loop due to the balance of the potential of the two lines, and the receiver in the telephone does not feel the sound from the telegraph machine. Similarly, when the telephone is communicating, the alternating current generated is also due to the thinning of the potential of the two lines and the capacitance of the capacitor in the telegraph circuit, so it does not disturb the work of the telegraph.

As for the connection of the complex circuit, it should be as shown in Figure B. 11 is a 50 ohm plug flow line wheel, 12 is a 30 ohm plug flow line wheel, C is a 2mF capacitor, R is a telegraph machine, and T is a telephone. The figure shows one telephone circuit and two telegraph circuits. The principle of this complex circuit is slightly different from that of a single circuit.

The principle is that the inductance number of the plug flow line wheel is large, the direct current is easy to pass through, and it is particularly difficult for high-frequency alternating current to pass through. On the other hand, the capacitor in the circuit has the opposite effect, that is, the alternating current passes through the capacitor without any obstruction, and if the direct current passes through, it will be cut off by it. In other words, the telephone current is a high-frequency alternating current, and it cannot flow through the circuit with a large inductance coefficient. At the same time, the telegraph current is a signal current, which is a direct current, and it is also impossible for it to pass through the circuit with the capacitor connected in series. According to this principle, the simultaneous telegraphy and telephony method of the complex circuit can be constructed.
